<div id="review_3043130185" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3043130185" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104765258-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573252975p2/104765258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3043130185?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/104765258-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104765258-david?shelf=_own">_own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104765258-david?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104765258-david?shelf=glbtq">glbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104765258-david?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3043130185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5351633893087892951"><i>24<br/>"You’re in a car with a beautiful boy, and he won’t tell you that he loves you, but he loves you. And you feel like you’ve done something terrible, like robbed a liquor store, or swallowed pills, or shoveled yourself a grave in the dirt, and you’re tired. You’re in a car with a beautiful boy, and you’re trying not to tell him that you love him, and you’re trying to choke down the feeling, and you’re trembling, but he reaches over and he touches you, like a prayer for which no words exist, and </i></span>
  <span id="freeText5351633893087892951" style="display:none"><i>24<br />"You’re in a car with a beautiful boy, and he won’t tell you that he loves you, but he loves you. And you feel like you’ve done something terrible, like robbed a liquor store, or swallowed pills, or shoveled yourself a grave in the dirt, and you’re tired. You’re in a car with a beautiful boy, and you’re trying not to tell him that you love him, and you’re trying to choke down the feeling, and you’re trembling, but he reaches over and he touches you, like a prayer for which no words exist, and you feel your heart taking root in your body, like you’ve discovered something you don’t even have a name for."</i><br /><br />This last panel from "You Are Jeff" concluded one of the best poems from this book. If you are a GR friend of mine, I have probably already sent you a poem (or 2, or 3) from this book as I've taken my time to read through it.<br /><br />From the first line of the first poem "Scheherazade":<br /><br /><i>"Tell me about the dream where we pull the bodies out of the lake and dress them in warm clothes again." </i><br /><br />to the conclusion of the last poem "Snow and Dirty Rain":<br /><br /><i>"My applejack, my silent night, just mash your lips against me. We are all going forward. None of us are going back."</i><br /><br />I've been in love with this collection!<br /><br />I found an interview with the author on line:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bombmagazine.org/articles/fight-club-richard-siken/">https://bombmagazine.org/articles/fig...</a><br /><br /><i>"Crush, at its core, is about rupture. The desire to touch, the gesture of touching, becomes dangerous, damaging, after the hand, withheld for so long, finally makes an attempt at contact. Simultaneously, and without pity, the natural world and its physical laws restrict the human form and its capacities. All of us are trapped in our skins and drowning in gravity. Physics is unforgiving. Nature is predatory. We do not walk through a passive landscape."</i><br /><br />Poetry, maybe more than most writing, speaks to everyone differently. It even speaks differently to the same person during different readings (time, place, reader). I am sure I will get more out of this collection as I continue to open this book again regularly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5351633893087892951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7497731438855907367">Powerful, painful and unique, Richard Siken's <i>Crush</i> was everything I'd hoped it would be. It's wordier than I usually prefer my poetry, but this was one of the few collections where I didn't mind the denser prose. Definitely going to check out more by him. <b>4/5</b></span>

<div id="review_529785674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/529785674" />
    <a title="Yara (The Narratologist)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4297791-yara-the-narratologist"><img alt="Yara (The Narratologist)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449173836p2/4297791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/529785674?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yara (The Narratologist)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yara (The Narratologist)" href="/user/show/4297791-yara-the-narratologist">Yara (The Narratologist)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4297791-yara-the-narratologist?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4297791-yara-the-narratologist?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4297791-yara-the-narratologist?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4297791-yara-the-narratologist?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529785674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14114265107300147077"><a href='http://www.thenarratologist.com/study-advice/study-advice-10-tips-approaching-poetry/' rel='nofollow noopener'>In an older study advice post on how to approach poetry,</a> I wrote that a good poet should be able to make you feel something, whether you fully understand the work or not:<br/><br/><blockquote>Often poems are not so much vessels of information, but more like an experience. A good poet can reach out and get an emotional response from you even if you have no clue what (s)he is talking about. Sometimes you need to read a poem a few times before you fully understand it, or you can spend the rest of your life reading a wor</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14114265107300147077" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.thenarratologist.com/study-advice/study-advice-10-tips-approaching-poetry/" rel="nofollow noopener">In an older study advice post on how to approach poetry,</a> I wrote that a good poet should be able to make you feel something, whether you fully understand the work or not:<br /><br /><blockquote>Often poems are not so much vessels of information, but more like an experience. A good poet can reach out and get an emotional response from you even if you have no clue what (s)he is talking about. Sometimes you need to read a poem a few times before you fully understand it, or you can spend the rest of your life reading a work and still not grasp what is actually about. Sometimes the poet doesn’t <i>want</i> you to get it. You’re not stupid or illiterate, it’s just… Poetry. If you feel it, you feel it. If you don’t, you don’t.</blockquote><br /><br />Even though Richard Siken is a fairly accessible poet, I had no idea what the poems in <i>Crush</i> were about the first time I read it, little over a year ago. But it didn’t matter, because I felt it. The words tugged on heartstrings I never even knew I had and left me staring out the window, trying to find the right words for the rush of emotions washing over me. I have read <i>Crush</i> two more times since then and I feel like I have a better grasp of it now, but it still leaves me staring out the window, at a complete loss for words.<br /><br />…But let’s give it a go anyway.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.thenarratologist.com/book-reviews/book-review-crush-2005-richard-siken/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Read More</b>
</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1053660514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1053660514" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10878292-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534503809p2/10878292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1053660514?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/10878292-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10878292-maddie?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10878292-maddie?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1053660514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13135275360587471347">I think reading a lot of Siken's poetry that came from this book before reading the book itself has caused me to not like it as much as I should, which is disappointing, and my mistake.<br/><br/>I've been left overwhelmed by Crush; there are poems in here that are some of my favourite in the world (<i>Snow and Dirty Rain</i>), lines that cut right through me but when you're reading a collection as opposed to individual poems, not all of them can hit so close. Some of them went on for a long time, dragging their </span>
  <span id="freeText13135275360587471347" style="display:none">I think reading a lot of Siken's poetry that came from this book before reading the book itself has caused me to not like it as much as I should, which is disappointing, and my mistake.<br /><br />I've been left overwhelmed by Crush; there are poems in here that are some of my favourite in the world (<i>Snow and Dirty Rain</i>), lines that cut right through me but when you're reading a collection as opposed to individual poems, not all of them can hit so close. Some of them went on for a long time, dragging their feet and I got too caught up in trying to follow to like them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13135275360587471347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sOnPIGZmkXDiTLLqGJoJOebcAzrEYYZ05A/rfz05Zowe6+/p+VyKzQLljJqUBVc5pmRqpHWpxI/Jy5Q7YLJc9w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

As he grows older, Geryon escapes his abusive brother and affectionate but ineffectual mother, finding solace behind the lens of his camera and in the arms of a young man named Herakles, a cavalier drifter who leaves him at the peak of infatuation. When Herakles reappears years later, Geryon confronts again the pain of his desire and embarks on a journey that will unleash his creative imagination to its fullest extent. By turns whimsical and haunting, erudite and accessible, richly layered and deceptively simple, Autobiography of Red is a profoundly moving portrait of an artist coming to terms with the fantastic accident of who he is.\n\n&quot;A profound love story . . . sensuous and funny, poignant, musical and tender.&quot; -- The New York Times Book Review\n\n&quot;A deeply odd and immensely engaging book. . . . 4,392 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2015\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11086726416781677792\">Bright Dead Things examines the chaos that is life, the dangerous thrill of living in a world you know you have to leave one day, and the search to find something that is ultimately “disorderly, and marvelous, and ours.”\n\nA book of bravado and intros<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11086726416781677792\" style=\"display:none\">Bright Dead Things examines the chaos that is life, the dangerous thrill of living in a world you know you have to leave one day, and the search to find something that is ultimately “disorderly, and marvelous, and ours.”\n\nA book of bravado and introspection, of 21st century feminist swagger and harrowing terror and loss, this fourth collection considers how we build our identities out of place and human contact—tracing in intimate detail the various ways the speaker’s sense of self both shifts and perseveres as she moves from New York City to rural Kentucky, loses a dear parent, ages past the capriciousness of youth, and falls in love. Limón has often been a poet who wears her heart on her sleeve, but in these extraordinary poems that heart becomes a “huge beating genius machine” striving to embrace and understand the fullness of the present moment. “I am beautiful. I am full of love. I am dying,” the poet writes. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14936897708576493149">Richard Siken is an American poet, painter, and filmmaker.<br/><br/>His poetry collection Crush won the 2004 Yale Series of Younger Poets prize, a Lambda Literary Award, the Thom Gunn Award, and was a finalist for the National Book Critics Circle Award. His poems have appeared in The Iowa Review, Conjunctions, Indiana Review and Forklift, Ohio, as well as in the anthologies The Best American Poetry 2000 and</span>
  <span id="freeText14936897708576493149" style="display:none">Richard Siken is an American poet, painter, and filmmaker.<br /><br />His poetry collection Crush won the 2004 Yale Series of Younger Poets prize, a Lambda Literary Award, the Thom Gunn Award, and was a finalist for the National Book Critics Circle Award. His poems have appeared in The Iowa Review, Conjunctions, Indiana Review and Forklift, Ohio, as well as in the anthologies The Best American Poetry 2000 and Legitimate Dangers. He is a recipient of a Pushcart Prize, two Arizona Commission on the Arts grants, and a fellowship from the National Endowment for the Arts.</span>
